I am not dreaming of any folly.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThey walked along in silence and only when they were close to\r\nRaskolnikov\xe2\x80\x99s lodgings, Razumihin broke the silence in considerable\r\nanxiety.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cListen,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cyou\xe2\x80\x99re a first-rate fellow, but among your other\r\nfailings, you\xe2\x80\x99re a loose fish, that I know, and a dirty one, too. You\r\nare a feeble, nervous wretch, and a mass of whims, you\xe2\x80\x99re getting fat\r\nand lazy and can\xe2\x80\x99t deny yourself anything--and I call that dirty because\r\nit leads one straight into the dirt. You\xe2\x80\x99ve let yourself get so slack\r\nthat I don\xe2\x80\x99t know how it is you are still a good, even a devoted doctor.\r\nYou--a doctor--sleep on a feather bed and get up at night to your\r\npatients! In another three or four years you won\xe2\x80\x99t get up for your\r\npatients... But hang it all, that\xe2\x80\x99s not the point!... You are going\r\nto spend to-night in the landlady\xe2\x80\x99s flat here. (Hard work I\xe2\x80\x99ve had to\r\npersuade her!) And I\xe2\x80\x99ll be in the kitchen. So here\xe2\x80\x99s a chance for you to\r\nget to know her better.... It\xe2\x80\x99s not as you think! There\xe2\x80\x99s not a trace of\r\nanything of the sort, brother...!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut I don\xe2\x80\x99t think!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHere you have modesty, brother, silence, bashfulness, a savage\r\nvirtue... and yet she\xe2\x80\x99s sighing and melting like wax, simply melting!\r\nSave me from her, by all that\xe2\x80\x99s unholy! She\xe2\x80\x99s most prepossessing... I\xe2\x80\x99ll\r\nrepay you, I\xe2\x80\x99ll do anything....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nZossimov laughed more violently than ever.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, you are smitten! But what am I to do with her?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt won\xe2\x80\x99t be much trouble, I assure you. Talk any rot you like to her,\r\nas long as you sit by her and talk. You\xe2\x80\x99re a doctor, too; try curing\r\nher of something. I swear you won\xe2\x80\x99t regret it. She has a piano, and you\r\nknow, I strum a little. I have a song there, a genuine Russian one: \xe2\x80\x98I\r\nshed hot tears.\xe2\x80\x99 She likes the genuine article--and well, it all\r\nbegan with that song; Now you\xe2\x80\x99re a regular performer, a _ma\xc3\xaetre_, a\r\nRubinstein.... I assure you, you won\xe2\x80\x99t regret it!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut have you made her some promise? Something signed? A promise of\r\nmarriage, perhaps?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNothing, nothing, absolutely nothing of the kind! Besides she is not\r\nthat sort at all.... Tchebarov tried that....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell then, drop her!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut I can\xe2\x80\x99t drop her like that!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy can\xe2\x80\x99t you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, I can\xe2\x80\x99t, that\xe2\x80\x99s all about it! There\xe2\x80\x99s an element of attraction\r\nhere, brother.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen why have you fascinated her?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI haven\xe2\x80\x99t fascinated her; perhaps I was fascinated myself in my folly.\r\nBut she won\xe2\x80\x99t care a straw whether it\xe2\x80\x99s you or I, so long as somebody\r\nsits beside her, sighing.... I can\xe2\x80\x99t explain the position, brother...\r\nlook here, you are good at mathematics, and working at it now... begin\r\nteaching her the integral calculus; upon my soul, I\xe2\x80\x99m not joking, I\xe2\x80\x99m\r\nin earnest, it\xe2\x80\x99ll be just the same to her. She will gaze at you and sigh\r\nfor a whole year together. I talked to her once for two days at a time\r\nabout the Prussian House of Lords (for one must talk of something)--she\r\njust sighed and perspired! And you mustn\xe2\x80\x99t talk of love--she\xe2\x80\x99s bashful\r\nto hysterics--but just let her see you can\xe2\x80\x99t tear yourself away--that\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nenough. It\xe2\x80\x99s fearfully comfortable; you\xe2\x80\x99re quite at home, you can\r\nread, sit, lie about, write. You may even venture on a kiss, if you\xe2\x80\x99re\r\ncareful.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what do I want with her?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAch, I can\xe2\x80\x99t make you understand! You see, you are made for each other!\r\nI have often been reminded of you!... You\xe2\x80\x99ll come to it in the end! So\r\ndoes it matter whether it\xe2\x80\x99s sooner or later? There\xe2\x80\x99s the feather-bed\r\nelement here, brother--ach! and not only that! There\xe2\x80\x99s an attraction\r\nhere--here you have the end of the world, an anchorage, a quiet haven,\r\nthe navel of the earth, the three fishes that are the foundation of the\r\nworld, the essence of pancakes, of savoury fish-pies, of the evening\r\nsamovar, of soft sighs and warm shawls, and hot stoves to sleep on--as\r\nsnug as though you were dead, and yet you\xe2\x80\x99re alive--the advantages\r\nof both at once! Well, hang it, brother, what stuff I\xe2\x80\x99m talking, it\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nbedtime! Listen. I sometimes wake up at night; so I\xe2\x80\x99ll go in and look at\r\nhim. But there\xe2\x80\x99s no need, it\xe2\x80\x99s all right. Don\xe2\x80\x99t you worry yourself,\r\nyet if you like, you might just look in once, too. But if you notice\r\nanything--delirium or fever--wake me at once. But there can\xe2\x80\x99t be....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCHAPTER II\r\n\r\nRazumihin waked up next morning at eight o\xe2\x80\x99clock, troubled and serious.\r\nHe found himself confronted with many new and unlooked-for perplexities.\r\nHe had never expected that he would ever wake up feeling like that. He\r\nremembered every detail of the previous day and he knew that a perfectly\r\nnovel experience had befallen him, that he had received an impression\r\nunlike anything he had known before. At the same time he recognised\r\nclearly that the dream which had fired his imagination was hopelessly\r\nunattainable--so unattainable that he felt positively ashamed of it, and\r\nhe hastened to pass to the other more practical cares and difficulties\r\nbequeathed him by that \xe2\x80\x9cthrice accursed yesterday.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe most awful recollection of the previous day was the way he had shown\r\nhimself \xe2\x80\x9cbase and mean,\xe2\x80\x9d not only because he had been drunk, but\r\nbecause he had taken advantage of the young girl\xe2\x80\x99s position to abuse\r\nher _fianc\xc3\xa9_ in his stupid jealousy, knowing nothing of their mutual\r\nrelations and obligations and next to nothing of the man himself. And\r\nwhat right had he to criticise him in that hasty and unguarded manner?\r\nWho had asked for his opinion? Was it thinkable that such a creature as\r\nAvdotya Romanovna would be marrying an unworthy man for money? So there\r\nmust be something in him. The lodgings? But after all how could he know\r\nthe character of the lodgings? He was furnishing a flat... Foo! how\r\ndespicable it all was! And what justification was it that he was drunk?\r\nSuch a stupid excuse was even more degrading! In wine is truth, and the\r\ntruth had all come out, \xe2\x80\x9cthat is, all the uncleanness of his coarse\r\nand envious heart\xe2\x80\x9d! And would such a dream ever be permissible to\r\nhim, Razumihin? What was he beside such a girl--he, the drunken noisy\r\nbraggart of last night? Was it possible to imagine so absurd and cynical\r\na juxtaposition? Razumihin blushed desperately at the very idea and\r\nsuddenly the recollection forced itself vividly upon him of how he had\r\nsaid last night on the stairs that the landlady would be jealous of\r\nAvdotya Romanovna... that was simply intolerable. He brought his fist\r\ndown heavily on the kitchen stove, hurt his hand and sent one of the\r\nbricks flying.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course,\xe2\x80\x9d he muttered to himself a minute later with a feeling of\r\nself-abasement, \xe2\x80\x9cof course, all these infamies can never be wiped out or\r\nsmoothed over... and so it\xe2\x80\x99s useless even to think of it, and I must\r\ngo to them in silence and do my duty... in silence, too... and not ask\r\nforgiveness, and say nothing... for all is lost now!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd yet as he dressed he examined his attire more carefully than usual.\r\nHe hadn\xe2\x80\x99t another suit--if he had had, perhaps he wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have put it\r\non. \xe2\x80\x9cI would have made a point of not putting it on.\xe2\x80\x9d But in any case he\r\ncould not remain a cynic and a dirty sloven; he had no right to offend\r\nthe feelings of others, especially when they were in need of his\r\nassistance and asking him to see them. He brushed his clothes carefully.\r\nHis linen was always decent; in that respect he was especially clean.\r\n\r\nHe washed that morning scrupulously--he got some soap from Nastasya--he\r\nwashed his hair, his neck and especially his hands. When it came to the\r\nquestion whether to shave his stubbly chin or not (Praskovya Pavlovna\r\nhad capital razors that had been left by her late husband), the question\r\nwas angrily answered in the negative. \xe2\x80\x9cLet it stay as it is! What if\r\nthey think that I shaved on purpose to...? They certainly would think\r\nso! Not on any account!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd... the worst of it was he was so coarse, so dirty, he had the\r\nmanners of a pothouse; and... and even admitting that he knew he had\r\nsome of the essentials of a gentleman... what was there in that to be\r\nproud of? Everyone ought to be a gentleman and more than that... and all\r\nthe same (he remembered) he, too, had done little things... not exactly\r\ndishonest, and yet.... And what thoughts he sometimes had; hm... and to\r\nset all that beside Avdotya Romanovna! Confound it! So be it! Well, he\xe2\x80\x99d\r\nmake a point then of being dirty, greasy, pothouse in his manners and he\r\nwouldn\xe2\x80\x99t care! He\xe2\x80\x99d be worse!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe was engaged in such monologues when Zossimov, who had spent the night\r\nin Praskovya Pavlovna\xe2\x80\x99s parlour, came in.\r\n\r\nHe was going home and was in a hurry to look at the invalid first.\r\nRazumihin informed him that Raskolnikov was sleeping like a dormouse.\r\nZossimov gave orders that they shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t wake him and promised to see\r\nhim again about eleven.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf he is still at home,\xe2\x80\x9d he added. \xe2\x80\x9cDamn it all! If one can\xe2\x80\x99t control\r\none\xe2\x80\x99s patients, how is one to cure them? Do you know whether _he_ will\r\ngo to them, or whether _they_ are coming here?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThey are coming, I think,\xe2\x80\x9d said Razumihin, understanding the object\r\nof the question, \xe2\x80\x9cand they will discuss their family affairs, no doubt.\r\nI\xe2\x80\x99ll be off. You, as the doctor, have more right to be here than I.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut I am not a father confessor; I shall come and go away; I\xe2\x80\x99ve plenty\r\nto do besides looking after them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOne thing worries me,\xe2\x80\x9d interposed Razumihin, frowning. \xe2\x80\x9cOn the way home\r\nI talked a lot of drunken nonsense to him... all sorts of things... and\r\namongst them that you were afraid that he... might become insane.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou told the ladies so, too.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI know it was stupid! You may beat me if you like! Did you think so\r\nseriously?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s nonsense, I tell you, how could I think it seriously? You,\r\nyourself, described him as a monomaniac when you fetched me to\r\nhim... and we added fuel to the fire yesterday, you did, that is, with\r\nyour story about the painter; it was a nice conversation, when he was,\r\nperhaps, mad on that very point! If only I\xe2\x80\x99d known what happened then\r\nat the police station and that some wretch... had insulted him with this\r\nsuspicion! Hm... I would not have allowed that conversation yesterday.\r\nThese monomaniacs will make a mountain out of a mole-hill... and\r\nsee their fancies as solid realities.... As far as I remember, it was\r\nZametov\xe2\x80\x99s story that cleared up half the mystery, to my mind. Why, I\r\nknow one case in which a hypochondriac, a man of forty, cut the throat\r\nof a little boy of eight, because he couldn\xe2\x80\x99t endure the jokes he made\r\nevery day at table! And in this case his rags, the insolent police\r\nofficer, the fever and this suspicion! All that working upon a man half\r\nfrantic with hypochondria, and with his morbid exceptional vanity! That\r\nmay well have been the starting-point of illness. Well, bother it\r\nall!... And, by the way, that Zametov certainly is a nice fellow, but\r\nhm... he shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have told all that last night. He is an awful\r\nchatterbox!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut whom did he tell it to? You and me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd Porfiry.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat does that matter?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd, by the way, have you any influence on them, his mother and sister?\r\nTell them to be more careful with him to-day....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99ll get on all right!\xe2\x80\x9d Razumihin answered reluctantly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy is he so set against this Luzhin? A man with money and she doesn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nseem to dislike him... and they haven\xe2\x80\x99t a farthing, I suppose? eh?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what business is it of yours?\xe2\x80\x9d Razumihin cried with annoyance. \xe2\x80\x9cHow\r\ncan I tell whether they\xe2\x80\x99ve a farthing? Ask them yourself and perhaps\r\nyou\xe2\x80\x99ll find out....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFoo! what an ass you are sometimes! Last night\xe2\x80\x99s wine has not gone off\r\nyet.... Good-bye; thank your Praskovya Pavlovna from me for my night\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nlodging. She locked herself in, made no reply to my _bonjour_ through\r\nthe door; she was up at seven o\xe2\x80\x99clock, the samovar was taken into her\r\nfrom the kitchen. I was not vouchsafed a personal interview....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAt nine o\xe2\x80\x99clock precisely Razumihin reached the lodgings at Bakaleyev\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nhouse. Both ladies were waiting for him with nervous impatience. They\r\nhad risen at seven o\xe2\x80\x99clock or earlier. He entered looking as black as\r\nnight, bowed awkwardly and was at once furious with himself for it. He\r\nhad reckoned without his host: Pulcheria Alexandrovna fairly rushed at\r\nhim, seized him by both hands and was almost kissing them. He glanced\r\ntimidly at Avdotya Romanovna, but her proud countenance wore at that\r\nmoment an expression of such gratitude and friendliness, such\r\ncomplete and unlooked-for respect (in place of the sneering looks and\r\nill-disguised contempt he had expected), that it threw him into greater\r\nconfusion than if he had been met with abuse. Fortunately there was a\r\nsubject for conversation, and he made haste to snatch at it.\r\n\r\nHearing that everything was going well and that Rodya had not yet waked,\r\nPulcheria Alexandrovna declared that she was glad to hear it, because\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cshe had something which it was very, very necessary to talk over\r\nbeforehand.\xe2\x80\x9d Then followed an inquiry about breakfast and an invitation\r\nto have it with them; they had waited to have it with him. Avdotya\r\nRomanovna rang the bell: it was answered by a ragged dirty waiter, and\r\nthey asked him to bring tea which was served at last, but in such\r\na dirty and disorderly way that the ladies were ashamed. Razumihin\r\nvigorously attacked the lodgings, but, remembering Luzhin, stopped\r\nin embarrassment and was greatly relieved by Pulcheria Alexandrovna\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nquestions, which showered in a continual stream upon him.\r\n\r\nHe talked for three quarters of an hour, being constantly interrupted\r\nby their questions, and succeeded in describing to them all the\r\nmost important facts he knew of the last year of Raskolnikov\xe2\x80\x99s life,\r\nconcluding with a circumstantial account of his illness. He omitted,\r\nhowever, many things, which were better omitted, including the scene at\r\nthe police station with all its consequences. They listened eagerly\r\nto his story, and, when he thought he had finished and satisfied his\r\nlisteners, he found that they considered he had hardly begun.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTell me, tell me! What do you think...? Excuse me, I still don\xe2\x80\x99t know\r\nyour name!\xe2\x80\x9d Pulcheria Alexandrovna put in hastily.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDmitri Prokofitch.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI should like very, very much to know, Dmitri Prokofitch... how he\r\nlooks... on things in general now, that is, how can I explain, what are\r\nhis likes and dislikes? Is he always so irritable? Tell me, if you can,\r\nwhat are his hopes and, so to say, his dreams? Under what influences is\r\nhe now? In a word, I should like...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh, mother, how can he answer all that at once?\xe2\x80\x9d observed Dounia.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood heavens, I had not expected to find him in the least like this,\r\nDmitri Prokofitch!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNaturally,\xe2\x80\x9d answered Razumihin. \xe2\x80\x9cI have no mother, but my uncle comes\r\nevery year and almost every time he can scarcely recognise me, even in\r\nappearance, though he is a clever man; and your three years\xe2\x80\x99 separation\r\nmeans a great deal. What am I to tell you? I have known Rodion for\r\na year and a half; he is morose, gloomy, proud and haughty, and of\r\nlate--and perhaps for a long time before--he has been suspicious and\r\nfanciful. He has a noble nature and a kind heart. He does not like\r\nshowing his feelings and would rather do a cruel thing than open his\r\nheart freely. Sometimes, though, he is not at all morbid, but simply\r\ncold and inhumanly callous; it\xe2\x80\x99s as though he were alternating between\r\ntwo characters. Sometimes he is fearfully reserved! He says he is\r\nso busy that everything is a hindrance, and yet he lies in bed doing\r\nnothing. He doesn\xe2\x80\x99t jeer at things, not because he hasn\xe2\x80\x99t the wit, but\r\nas though he hadn\xe2\x80\x99t time to waste on such trifles. He never listens\r\nto what is said to him. He is never interested in what interests other\r\npeople at any given moment. He thinks very highly of himself and perhaps\r\nhe is right. Well, what more? I think your arrival will have a most\r\nbeneficial influence upon him.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGod grant it may,\xe2\x80\x9d cried Pulcheria Alexandrovna, distressed by\r\nRazumihin\xe2\x80\x99s account of her Rodya.\r\n\r\nAnd Razumihin ventured to look more boldly at Avdotya Romanovna at last.\r\nHe glanced at her often while he was talking, but only for a moment and\r\nlooked away again at once. Avdotya Romanovna sat at the table, listening\r\nattentively, then got up again and began walking to and fro with her\r\narms folded and her lips compressed, occasionally putting in a question,\r\nwithout stopping her walk. She had the same habit of not listening to\r\nwhat was said. She was wearing a dress of thin dark stuff and she had a\r\nwhite transparent scarf round her neck. Razumihin soon detected signs of\r\nextreme poverty in their belongings. Had Avdotya Romanovna been dressed\r\nlike a queen, he felt that he would not be afraid of her, but perhaps\r\njust because she was poorly dressed and that he noticed all the misery\r\nof her surroundings, his heart was filled with dread and he began to be\r\nafraid of every word he uttered, every gesture he made, which was very\r\ntrying for a man who already felt diffident.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99ve told us a great deal that is interesting about my brother\xe2\x80\x99s\r\ncharacter... and have told it impartially. I am glad. I thought that you\r\nwere too uncritically devoted to him,\xe2\x80\x9d observed Avdotya Romanovna with\r\na smile. \xe2\x80\x9cI think you are right that he needs a woman\xe2\x80\x99s care,\xe2\x80\x9d she added\r\nthoughtfully.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI didn\xe2\x80\x99t say so; but I daresay you are right, only...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe loves no one and perhaps he never will,\xe2\x80\x9d Razumihin declared\r\ndecisively.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou mean he is not capable of love?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you know, Avdotya Romanovna, you are awfully like your brother, in\r\neverything, indeed!\xe2\x80\x9d he blurted out suddenly to his own surprise, but\r\nremembering at once what he had just before said of her brother,\r\nhe turned as red as a crab and was overcome with confusion. Avdotya\r\nRomanovna couldn\xe2\x80\x99t help laughing when she looked at him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou may both be mistaken about Rodya,\xe2\x80\x9d Pulcheria Alexandrovna remarked,\r\nslightly piqued. \xe2\x80\x9cI am not talking of our present difficulty, Dounia.\r\nWhat Pyotr Petrovitch writes in this letter and what you and I have\r\nsupposed may be mistaken, but you can\xe2\x80\x99t imagine, Dmitri Prokofitch, how\r\nmoody and, so to say, capricious he is. I never could depend on what\r\nhe would do when he was only fifteen. And I am sure that he might\r\ndo something now that nobody else would think of doing... Well, for\r\ninstance, do you know how a year and a half ago he astounded me and gave\r\nme a shock that nearly killed me, when he had the idea of marrying that\r\ngirl--what was her name--his landlady\xe2\x80\x99s daughter?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDid you hear about that affair?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Avdotya Romanovna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you suppose----\xe2\x80\x9d Pulcheria Alexandrovna continued warmly. \xe2\x80\x9cDo you\r\nsuppose that my tears, my entreaties, my illness, my possible death from\r\ngrief, our poverty would have made him pause? No, he would calmly have\r\ndisregarded all obstacles. And yet it isn\xe2\x80\x99t that he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t love us!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe has never spoken a word of that affair to me,\xe2\x80\x9d Razumihin answered\r\ncautiously. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I did hear something from Praskovya Pavlovna herself,\r\nthough she is by no means a gossip. And what I heard certainly was\r\nrather strange.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd what did you hear?\xe2\x80\x9d both the ladies asked at once.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, nothing very special. I only learned that the marriage, which\r\nonly failed to take place through the girl\xe2\x80\x99s death, was not at all to\r\nPraskovya Pavlovna\xe2\x80\x99s liking. They say, too, the girl was not at all\r\npretty, in fact I am told positively ugly... and such an invalid... and\r\nqueer. But she seems to have had some good qualities. She must have\r\nhad some good qualities or it\xe2\x80\x99s quite inexplicable.... She had no money\r\neither and he wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have considered her money.... But it\xe2\x80\x99s always\r\ndifficult to judge in such matters.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am sure she was a good girl,\xe2\x80\x9d Avdotya Romanovna observed briefly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGod forgive me, I simply rejoiced at her death. Though I don\xe2\x80\x99t know\r\nwhich of them would have caused most misery to the other--he to her\r\nor she to him,\xe2\x80\x9d Pulcheria Alexandrovna concluded. Then she began\r\ntentatively questioning him about the scene on the previous day with\r\nLuzhin, hesitating and continually glancing at Dounia, obviously to\r\nthe latter\xe2\x80\x99s annoyance. This incident more than all the rest evidently\r\ncaused her uneasiness, even consternation. Razumihin described it in\r\ndetail again, but this time he added his own conclusions: he openly\r\nblamed Raskolnikov for intentionally insulting Pyotr Petrovitch, not\r\nseeking to excuse him on the score of his illness.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe had planned it before his illness,\xe2\x80\x9d he added.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think so, too,\xe2\x80\x9d Pulcheria Alexandrovna agreed with a dejected air.\r\nBut she was very much surprised at hearing Razumihin express himself\r\nso carefully and even with a certain respect about Pyotr Petrovitch.\r\nAvdotya Romanovna, too, was struck by it.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo this is your opinion of Pyotr Petrovitch?\xe2\x80\x9d Pulcheria Alexandrovna\r\ncould not resist asking.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can have no other opinion of your daughter\xe2\x80\x99s future husband,\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n Razumihin answered firmly and with warmth, \xe2\x80\x9cand I don\xe2\x80\x99t say it simply\r\nfrom vulgar politeness, but because... simply because Avdotya Romanovna\r\nhas of her own free will deigned to accept this man. If I spoke so\r\nrudely of him last night, it was because I was disgustingly drunk and...\r\nmad besides; yes, mad, crazy, I lost my head completely... and this\r\nmorning I am ashamed of it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe crimsoned and ceased speaking. Avdotya Romanovna flushed, but did not\r\nbreak the silence. She had not uttered a word from the moment they began\r\nto speak of Luzhin.\r\n\r\nWithout her support Pulcheria Alexandrovna obviously did not know what\r\nto do. At last, faltering and continually glancing at her daughter, she\r\nconfessed that she was exceedingly worried by one circumstance.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou see, Dmitri Prokofitch,\xe2\x80\x9d she began. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll be perfectly open with\r\nDmitri Prokofitch, Dounia?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course, mother,\xe2\x80\x9d said Avdotya Romanovna emphatically.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is what it is,\xe2\x80\x9d she began in haste, as though the permission to\r\nspeak of her trouble lifted a weight off her mind. \xe2\x80\x9cVery early this\r\nmorning we got a note from Pyotr Petrovitch in reply to our letter\r\nannouncing our arrival. He promised to meet us at the station, you\r\nknow; instead of that he sent a servant to bring us the address of these\r\nlodgings and to show us the way; and he sent a message that he would\r\nbe here himself this morning. But this morning this note came from him.\r\nYou\xe2\x80\x99d better read it yourself; there is one point in it which worries me\r\nvery much... you will soon see what that is, and... tell me your candid\r\nopinion, Dmitri Prokofitch! You know Rodya\xe2\x80\x99s character better than\r\nanyone and no one can advise us better than you can. Dounia, I must tell\r\nyou, made her decision at once, but I still don\xe2\x80\x99t feel sure how to act\r\nand I... I\xe2\x80\x99ve been waiting for your opinion.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nRazumihin opened the note which was dated the previous evening and read\r\nas follows:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDear Madam, Pulcheria Alexandrovna, I have the honour to inform you\r\nthat owing to unforeseen obstacles I was rendered unable to meet you at\r\nthe railway station; I sent a very competent person with the same object\r\nin view. I likewise shall be deprived of the honour of an interview with\r\nyou to-morrow morning by business in the Senate that does not admit of\r\ndelay, and also that I may not intrude on your family circle while you\r\nare meeting your son, and Avdotya Romanovna her brother. I shall have\r\nthe honour of visiting you and paying you my respects at your lodgings\r\nnot later than to-morrow evening at eight o\xe2\x80\x99clock precisely, and\r\nherewith I venture to present my earnest and, I may add, imperative\r\nrequest that Rodion Romanovitch may not be present at our interview--as\r\nhe offered me a gross and unprecedented affront on the occasion of my\r\nvisit to him in his illness yesterday, and, moreover, since I desire\r\nfrom you personally an indispensable and circumstantial explanation\r\nupon a certain point, in regard to which I wish to learn your own\r\ninterpretation. I have the honour to inform you, in anticipation,\r\nthat if, in spite of my request, I meet Rodion Romanovitch, I shall be\r\ncompelled to withdraw immediately and then you have only yourself to\r\nblame. I write on the assumption that Rodion Romanovitch who appeared so\r\nill at my visit, suddenly recovered two hours later and so, being able\r\nto leave the house, may visit you also. I was confirmed in that belief\r\nby the testimony of my own eyes in the lodging of a drunken man who\r\nwas run over and has since died, to whose daughter, a young woman of\r\nnotorious behaviour, he gave twenty-five roubles on the pretext of the\r\nfuneral, which gravely surprised me knowing what pains you were at to\r\nraise that sum. Herewith expressing my special respect to your estimable\r\ndaughter, Avdotya Romanovna, I beg you to accept the respectful homage\r\nof\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYour humble servant,\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cP. LUZHIN.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat am I to do now, Dmitri Prokofitch?\xe2\x80\x9d began Pulcheria Alexandrovna,\r\nalmost weeping. \xe2\x80\x9cHow can I ask Rodya not to come? Yesterday he insisted\r\nso earnestly on our refusing Pyotr Petrovitch and now we are ordered not\r\nto receive Rodya! He will come on purpose if he knows, and... what will\r\nhappen then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAct on Avdotya Romanovna\xe2\x80\x99s decision,\xe2\x80\x9d Razumihin answered calmly at\r\nonce.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, dear me! She says... goodness knows what she says, she doesn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nexplain her object! She says that it would be best, at least, not that\r\nit would be best, but that it\xe2\x80\x99s absolutely necessary that Rodya should\r\nmake a point of being here at eight o\xe2\x80\x99clock and that they must meet....\r\nI didn\xe2\x80\x99t want even to show him the letter, but to prevent him\r\nfrom coming by some stratagem with your help... because he is so\r\nirritable.... Besides I don\xe2\x80\x99t understand about that drunkard who died\r\nand that daughter, and how he could have given the daughter all the\r\nmoney... which...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhich cost you such sacrifice, mother,\xe2\x80\x9d put in Avdotya Romanovna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe was not himself yesterday,\xe2\x80\x9d Razumihin said thoughtfully, \xe2\x80\x9cif you\r\nonly knew what he was up to in a restaurant yesterday, though there\r\nwas sense in it too.... Hm! He did say something, as we were going home\r\nyesterday evening, about a dead man and a girl, but I didn\xe2\x80\x99t understand\r\na word.... But last night, I myself...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe best thing, mother, will be for us to go to him ourselves and\r\nthere I assure you we shall see at once what\xe2\x80\x99s to be done. Besides,\r\nit\xe2\x80\x99s getting late--good heavens, it\xe2\x80\x99s past ten,\xe2\x80\x9d she cried looking at\r\na splendid gold enamelled watch which hung round her neck on a thin\r\nVenetian chain, and looked entirely out of keeping with the rest of her\r\ndress. \xe2\x80\x9cA present from her _fianc\xc3\xa9_,\xe2\x80\x9d thought Razumihin.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe must start, Dounia, we must start,\xe2\x80\x9d her mother cried in a flutter.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe will be thinking we are still angry after yesterday, from our coming\r\nso late. Merciful heavens!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWhile she said this she was hurriedly putting on her hat and mantle;\r\nDounia, too, put on her things. Her gloves, as Razumihin noticed, were\r\nnot merely shabby but had holes in them, and yet this evident poverty\r\ngave the two ladies an air of special dignity, which is always found in\r\npeople who know how to wear poor clothes. Razumihin looked reverently\r\nat Dounia and felt proud of escorting her. \xe2\x80\x9cThe queen who mended her\r\nstockings in prison,\xe2\x80\x9d he thought, \xe2\x80\x9cmust have looked then every inch a\r\nqueen and even more a queen than at sumptuous banquets and lev\xc3\xa9es.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy God!\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Pulcheria Alexandrovna, \xe2\x80\x9clittle did I think that I\r\nshould ever fear seeing my son, my darling, darling Rodya! I am afraid,\r\nDmitri Prokofitch,\xe2\x80\x9d she added, glancing at him timidly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t be afraid, mother,\xe2\x80\x9d said Dounia, kissing her, \xe2\x80\x9cbetter have faith\r\nin him.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, dear, I have faith in him, but I haven\xe2\x80\x99t slept all night,\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n exclaimed the poor woman.\r\n\r\nThey came out into the street.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you know, Dounia, when I dozed a little this morning I dreamed of\r\nMarfa Petrovna... she was all in white... she came up to me, took\r\nmy hand, and shook her head at me, but so sternly as though she were\r\nblaming me.... Is that a good omen? Oh, dear me! You don\xe2\x80\x99t know, Dmitri\r\nProkofitch, that Marfa Petrovna\xe2\x80\x99s dead!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, I didn\xe2\x80\x99t know; who is Marfa Petrovna?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe died suddenly; and only fancy...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAfterwards, mamma,\xe2\x80\x9d put in Dounia. \xe2\x80\x9cHe doesn\xe2\x80\x99t know who Marfa Petrovna\r\nis.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh, you don\xe2\x80\x99t know? And I was thinking that you knew all about us.\r\nForgive me, Dmitri Prokofitch, I don\xe2\x80\x99t know what I am thinking about\r\nthese last few days. I look upon you really as a providence for us, and\r\nso I took it for granted that you knew all about us. I look on you as a\r\nrelation.... Don\xe2\x80\x99t be angry with me for saying so. Dear me, what\xe2\x80\x99s the\r\nmatter with your right hand? Have you knocked it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, I bruised it,\xe2\x80\x9d muttered Razumihin overjoyed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI sometimes speak too much from the heart, so that Dounia finds fault\r\nwith me.... But, dear me, what a cupboard he lives in! I wonder whether\r\nhe is awake? Does this woman, his landlady, consider it a room? Listen,\r\nyou say he does not like to show his feelings, so perhaps I shall annoy\r\nhim with my... weaknesses? Do advise me, Dmitri Prokofitch, how am I to\r\ntreat him? I feel quite distracted, you know.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t question him too much about anything if you see him frown; don\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nask him too much about his health; he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t like that.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh, Dmitri Prokofitch, how hard it is to be a mother! But here are the\r\nstairs.... What an awful staircase!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMother, you are quite pale, don\xe2\x80\x99t distress yourself, darling,\xe2\x80\x9d said\r\nDounia caressing her, then with flashing eyes she added: \xe2\x80\x9cHe ought to be\r\nhappy at seeing you, and you are tormenting yourself so.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWait, I\xe2\x80\x99ll peep in and see whether he has waked up.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe ladies slowly followed Razumihin, who went on before, and when they\r\nreached the landlady\xe2\x80\x99s door on the fourth storey, they noticed that her\r\ndoor was a tiny crack open and that two keen black eyes were watching\r\nthem from the darkness within. When their eyes met, the door was\r\nsuddenly shut with such a slam that Pulcheria Alexandrovna almost cried\r\nout.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCHAPTER III\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe is well, quite well!\xe2\x80\x9d Zossimov cried cheerfully as they entered.\r\n\r\nHe had come in ten minutes earlier and was sitting in the same place\r\nas before, on the sofa. Raskolnikov was sitting in the opposite corner,\r\nfully dressed and carefully washed and combed, as he had not been for\r\nsome time past. The room was immediately crowded, yet Nastasya managed\r\nto follow the visitors in and stayed to listen.\r\n\r\nRaskolnikov really was almost well, as compared with his condition the\r\nday before, but he was still pale, listless, and sombre. He looked like\r\na wounded man or one who has undergone some terrible physical suffering.\r\nHis brows were knitted, his lips compressed, his eyes feverish. He spoke\r\nlittle and reluctantly, as though performing a duty, and there was a\r\nrestlessness in his movements.\r\n\r\nHe only wanted a sling on his arm or a bandage on his finger to complete\r\nthe impression of a man with a painful abscess or a broken arm. The\r\npale, sombre face lighted up for a moment when his mother and sister\r\nentered, but this only gave it a look of more intense suffering, in\r\nplace of its listless dejection. The light soon died away, but the look\r\nof suffering remained, and Zossimov, watching and studying his patient\r\nwith all the zest of a young doctor beginning to practise, noticed\r\nin him no joy at the arrival of his mother and sister, but a sort of\r\nbitter, hidden determination to bear another hour or two of inevitable\r\ntorture. He saw later that almost every word of the following\r\nconversation seemed to touch on some sore place and irritate it. But\r\nat the same time he marvelled at the power of controlling himself\r\nand hiding his feelings in a patient who the previous day had, like a\r\nmonomaniac, fallen into a frenzy at the slightest word.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, I see myself now that I am almost well,\xe2\x80\x9d said Raskolnikov,\r\ngiving his mother and sister a kiss of welcome which made Pulcheria\r\nAlexandrovna radiant at once. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd I don\xe2\x80\x99t say this _as I did\r\nyesterday_,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, addressing Razumihin, with a friendly pressure of\r\nhis hand.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, indeed, I am quite surprised at him to-day,\xe2\x80\x9d began Zossimov, much\r\ndelighted at the ladies\xe2\x80\x99 entrance, for he had not succeeded in keeping\r\nup a conversation with his patient for ten minutes. \xe2\x80\x9cIn another three or\r\nfour days, if he goes on like this, he will be just as before, that is,\r\nas he was a month ago, or two... or perhaps even three. This has been\r\ncoming on for a long while.... eh? Confess, now, that it has been\r\nperhaps your own fault?\xe2\x80\x9d he added, with a tentative smile, as though\r\nstill afraid of irritating him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is very possible,\xe2\x80\x9d answered Raskolnikov coldly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI should say, too,\xe2\x80\x9d continued Zossimov with zest, \xe2\x80\x9cthat your complete\r\nrecovery depends solely on yourself. Now that one can talk to you,\r\nI should like to impress upon you that it is essential to avoid the\r\nelementary, so to speak, fundamental causes tending to produce your\r\nmorbid condition: in that case you will be cured, if not, it will go\r\nfrom bad to worse. These fundamental causes I don\xe2\x80\x99t know, but they must\r\nbe known to you. You are an intelligent man, and must have observed\r\nyourself, of course. I fancy the first stage of your derangement\r\ncoincides with your leaving the university. You must not be left without\r\noccupation, and so, work and a definite aim set before you might, I\r\nfancy, be very beneficial.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, yes; you are perfectly right.... I will make haste and return to\r\nthe university: and then everything will go smoothly....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nZossimov, who had begun his sage advice partly to make an effect before\r\nthe ladies, was certainly somewhat mystified, when, glancing at his\r\npatient, he observed unmistakable mockery on his face. This lasted\r\nan instant, however. Pulcheria Alexandrovna began at once thanking\r\nZossimov, especially for his visit to their lodging the previous night.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat! he saw you last night?\xe2\x80\x9d Raskolnikov asked, as though startled.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen you have not slept either after your journey.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAch, Rodya, that was only till two o\xe2\x80\x99clock. Dounia and I never go to\r\nbed before two at home.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t know how to thank him either,\xe2\x80\x9d Raskolnikov went on,\r\nsuddenly frowning and looking down. \xe2\x80\x9cSetting aside the question of\r\npayment--forgive me for referring to it (he turned to Zossimov)--I\r\nreally don\xe2\x80\x99t know what I have done to deserve such special attention\r\nfrom you! I simply don\xe2\x80\x99t understand it... and... and... it weighs upon\r\nme, indeed, because I don\xe2\x80\x99t understand it. I tell you so candidly.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t be irritated.\xe2\x80\x9d Zossimov forced himself to laugh. \xe2\x80\x9cAssume that you\r\nare my first patient--well--we fellows just beginning to practise love\r\nour first patients as if they were our children, and some almost fall in\r\nlove with them. And, of course, I am not rich in patients.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI say nothing about him,\xe2\x80\x9d added Raskolnikov, pointing to Razumihin,\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cthough he has had nothing from me either but insult and trouble.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat nonsense he is talking! Why, you are in a sentimental mood to-day,\r\nare you?\xe2\x80\x9d shouted Razumihin.\r\n\r\nIf he had had more penetration he would have seen that there was no\r\ntrace of sentimentality in him, but something indeed quite the opposite.\r\nBut Avdotya Romanovna noticed it. She was intently and uneasily watching\r\nher brother.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAs for you, mother, I don\xe2\x80\x99t dare to speak,\xe2\x80\x9d he went on, as though\r\nrepeating a lesson learned by heart. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is only to-day that I have\r\nbeen able to realise a little how distressed you must have been here\r\nyesterday, waiting for me to come back.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWhen he had said this, he suddenly held out his hand to his sister,\r\nsmiling without a word. But in this smile there was a flash of real\r\nunfeigned feeling. Dounia caught it at once, and warmly pressed his\r\nhand, overjoyed and thankful. It was the first time he had addressed her\r\nsince their dispute the previous day. The mother\xe2\x80\x99s face lighted up\r\nwith ecstatic happiness at the sight of this conclusive unspoken\r\nreconciliation. \xe2\x80\x9cYes, that is what I love him for,\xe2\x80\x9d Razumihin,\r\nexaggerating it all, muttered to himself, with a vigorous turn in his\r\nchair. \xe2\x80\x9cHe has these movements.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd how well he does it all,\xe2\x80\x9d the mother was thinking to herself. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat\r\ngenerous impulses he has, and how simply, how delicately he put an end\r\nto all the misunderstanding with his sister--simply by holding out his\r\nhand at the right minute and looking at her like that.... And what\r\nfine eyes he has, and how fine his whole face is!... He is even better\r\nlooking than Dounia.... But, good heavens, what a suit--how terribly\r\nhe\xe2\x80\x99s dressed!... Vasya, the messenger boy in Afanasy Ivanitch\xe2\x80\x99s shop, is\r\nbetter dressed! I could rush at him and hug him... weep over him--but\r\nI am afraid.... Oh, dear, he\xe2\x80\x99s so strange! He\xe2\x80\x99s talking kindly, but I\xe2\x80\x99m\r\nafraid! Why, what am I afraid of?...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, Rodya, you wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t believe,\xe2\x80\x9d she began suddenly, in haste to\r\nanswer his words to her, \xe2\x80\x9chow unhappy Dounia and I were yesterday! Now\r\nthat it\xe2\x80\x99s all over and done with and we are quite happy again--I can\r\ntell you. Fancy, we ran here almost straight from the train to embrace\r\nyou and that woman--ah, here she is! Good morning, Nastasya!... She told\r\nus at once that you were lying in a high fever and had just run away\r\nfrom the doctor in delirium, and they were looking for you in the\r\nstreets. You can\xe2\x80\x99t imagine how we felt! And even if you were right, if I really had determined on a\r\nvile action, is it not merciless on your part to speak to me like that?\r\nWhy do you demand of me a heroism that perhaps you have not either? It\r\nis despotism; it is tyranny. If I ruin anyone, it is only myself.... I\r\nam not committing a murder. Why do you look at me like that? Why are you\r\nso pale? Rodya, darling, what\xe2\x80\x99s the matter?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood heavens! You have made him faint,\xe2\x80\x9d cried Pulcheria Alexandrovna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, no, nonsense! It\xe2\x80\x99s nothing. A little giddiness--not fainting. You\r\nhave fainting on the brain. H\xe2\x80\x99m, yes, what was I saying? Oh, yes. In\r\nwhat way will you get convincing proof to-day that you can respect him,\r\nand that he... esteems you, as you said. I think you said to-day?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMother, show Rodya Pyotr Petrovitch\xe2\x80\x99s letter,\xe2\x80\x9d said Dounia.\r\n\r\nWith trembling hands, Pulcheria Alexandrovna gave him the letter. He\r\ntook it with great interest, but, before opening it, he suddenly looked\r\nwith a sort of wonder at Dounia.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is strange,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, slowly, as though struck by a new idea. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat\r\nam I making such a fuss for? What is it all about? Marry whom you like!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe said this as though to himself, but said it aloud, and looked for\r\nsome time at his sister, as though puzzled. He opened the letter at\r\nlast, still with the same look of strange wonder on his face. Then,\r\nslowly and attentively, he began reading, and read it through twice.\r\nPulcheria Alexandrovna showed marked anxiety, and all indeed expected\r\nsomething particular.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat surprises me,\xe2\x80\x9d he began, after a short pause, handing the letter\r\nto his mother, but not addressing anyone in particular, \xe2\x80\x9cis that he is a\r\nbusiness man, a lawyer, and his conversation is pretentious indeed, and\r\nyet he writes such an uneducated letter.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThey all started. They had expected something quite different.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut they all write like that, you know,\xe2\x80\x9d Razumihin observed, abruptly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHave you read it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe showed him, Rodya. We... consulted him just now,\xe2\x80\x9d Pulcheria\r\nAlexandrovna began, embarrassed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s just the jargon of the courts,\xe2\x80\x9d Razumihin put in. \xe2\x80\x9cLegal\r\ndocuments are written like that to this day.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLegal? Yes, it\xe2\x80\x99s just legal--business language--not so very uneducated,\r\nand not quite educated--business language!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPyotr Petrovitch makes no secret of the fact that he had a cheap\r\neducation, he is proud indeed of having made his own way,\xe2\x80\x9d Avdotya\r\nRomanovna observed, somewhat offended by her brother\xe2\x80\x99s tone.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, if he\xe2\x80\x99s proud of it, he has reason, I don\xe2\x80\x99t deny it. You seem to\r\nbe offended, sister, at my making only such a frivolous criticism on the\r\nletter, and to think that I speak of such trifling matters on purpose to\r\nannoy you. It is quite the contrary, an observation apropos of the style\r\noccurred to me that is by no means irrelevant as things stand. There\r\nis one expression, \xe2\x80\x98blame yourselves\xe2\x80\x99 put in very significantly and\r\nplainly, and there is besides a threat that he will go away at once if I\r\nam present. That threat to go away is equivalent to a threat to abandon\r\nyou both if you are disobedient, and to abandon you now after summoning\r\nyou to Petersburg. Well, what do you think? Can one resent such an\r\nexpression from Luzhin, as we should if he (he pointed to Razumihin) had\r\nwritten it, or Zossimov, or one of us?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cN-no,\xe2\x80\x9d answered Dounia, with more animation. \xe2\x80\x9cI saw clearly that it\r\nwas too na\xc3\xafvely expressed, and that perhaps he simply has no skill\r\nin writing... that is a true criticism, brother. I did not expect,\r\nindeed...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is expressed in legal style, and sounds coarser than perhaps he\r\nintended. But I must disillusion you a little. There is one expression\r\nin the letter, one slander about me, and rather a contemptible one. I\r\ngave the money last night to the widow, a woman in consumption, crushed\r\nwith trouble, and not \xe2\x80\x98on the pretext of the funeral,\xe2\x80\x99 but simply to pay\r\nfor the funeral, and not to the daughter--a young woman, as he writes,\r\nof notorious behaviour (whom I saw last night for the first time in my\r\nlife)--but to the widow. In all this I see a too hasty desire to slander\r\nme and to raise dissension between us. It is expressed again in legal\r\njargon, that is to say, with a too obvious display of the aim, and\r\nwith a very na\xc3\xafve eagerness. He is a man of intelligence, but to act\r\nsensibly, intelligence is not enough. It all shows the man and... I\r\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t think he has a great esteem for you. I tell you this simply to\r\nwarn you, because I sincerely wish for your good...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nDounia did not reply. Her resolution had been taken. She was only\r\nawaiting the evening.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen what is your decision, Rodya?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Pulcheria Alexandrovna, who\r\nwas more uneasy than ever at the sudden, new businesslike tone of his\r\ntalk.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat decision?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou see Pyotr Petrovitch writes that you are not to be with us this\r\nevening, and that he will go away if you come. So will you... come?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat, of course, is not for me to decide, but for you first, if you are\r\nnot offended by such a request; and secondly, by Dounia, if she, too, is\r\nnot offended. I will do what you think best,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, drily.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDounia has already decided, and I fully agree with her,\xe2\x80\x9d Pulcheria\r\nAlexandrovna hastened to declare.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI decided to ask you, Rodya, to urge you not to fail to be with us at\r\nthis interview,\xe2\x80\x9d said Dounia. \xe2\x80\x9cWill you come?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI will ask you, too, to be with us at eight o\xe2\x80\x99clock,\xe2\x80\x9d she said,\r\naddressing Razumihin. \xe2\x80\x9cMother, I am inviting him, too.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cQuite right, Dounia. Well, since you have decided,\xe2\x80\x9d added Pulcheria\r\nAlexandrovna, \xe2\x80\x9cso be it. I shall feel easier myself. I do not like\r\nconcealment and deception. Better let us have the whole truth.... Pyotr\r\nPetrovitch may be angry or not, now!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCHAPTER IV\r\n\r\nAt that moment the door was softly opened, and a young girl walked into\r\nthe room, looking timidly about her. Everyone turned towards her with\r\nsurprise and curiosity. At first sight, Raskolnikov did not recognise\r\nher. It was Sofya Semyonovna Marmeladov. He had seen her yesterday for\r\nthe first time, but at such a moment, in such surroundings and in such\r\na dress, that his memory retained a very different image of her. Now she\r\nwas a modestly and poorly-dressed young girl, very young, indeed,\r\nalmost like a child, with a modest and refined manner, with a candid but\r\nsomewhat frightened-looking face. She was wearing a very plain indoor\r\ndress, and had on a shabby old-fashioned hat, but she still carried a\r\nparasol. Unexpectedly finding the room full of people, she was not so\r\nmuch embarrassed as completely overwhelmed with shyness, like a\r\nlittle child. She was even about to retreat. \xe2\x80\x9cOh... it\xe2\x80\x99s you!\xe2\x80\x9d said\r\nRaskolnikov, extremely astonished, and he, too, was confused. He at once\r\nrecollected that his mother and sister knew through Luzhin\xe2\x80\x99s letter\r\nof \xe2\x80\x9csome young woman of notorious behaviour.\xe2\x80\x9d He had only just been\r\nprotesting against Luzhin\xe2\x80\x99s calumny and declaring that he had seen the\r\ngirl last night for the first time, and suddenly she had walked in. He\r\nremembered, too, that he had not protested against the expression \xe2\x80\x9cof\r\nnotorious behaviour.\xe2\x80\x9d All this passed vaguely and fleetingly through\r\nhis brain, but looking at her more intently, he saw that the humiliated\r\ncreature was so humiliated that he felt suddenly sorry for her. When she\r\nmade a movement to retreat in terror, it sent a pang to his heart.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI did not expect you,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, hurriedly, with a look that made her\r\nstop. \xe2\x80\x9cPlease sit down. You come, no doubt, from Katerina Ivanovna.\r\nAllow me--not there. Sit here....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAt Sonia\xe2\x80\x99s entrance, Razumihin, who had been sitting on one of\r\nRaskolnikov\xe2\x80\x99s three chairs, close to the door, got up to allow her to\r\nenter. Raskolnikov had at first shown her the place on the sofa where\r\nZossimov had been sitting, but feeling that the sofa which served him\r\nas a bed, was too _familiar_ a place, he hurriedly motioned her to\r\nRazumihin\xe2\x80\x99s chair.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou sit here,\xe2\x80\x9d he said to Razumihin, putting him on the sofa.\r\n\r\nSonia sat down, almost shaking with terror, and looked timidly at the\r\ntwo ladies. It was evidently almost inconceivable to herself that she\r\ncould sit down beside them. At the thought of it, she was so frightened\r\nthat she hurriedly got up again, and in utter confusion addressed\r\nRaskolnikov.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI... I... have come for one minute. Forgive me for disturbing you,\xe2\x80\x9d she\r\nbegan falteringly. \xe2\x80\x9cI come from Katerina Ivanovna, and she had no one to\r\nsend. Katerina Ivanovna told me to beg you... to be at the service... in\r\nthe morning... at Mitrofanievsky... and then... to us... to her...\r\nto do her the honour... she told me to beg you...\xe2\x80\x9d Sonia stammered and\r\nceased speaking.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI will try, certainly, most certainly,\xe2\x80\x9d answered Raskolnikov. He,\r\ntoo, stood up, and he, too, faltered and could not finish his sentence.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPlease sit down,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, suddenly. \xe2\x80\x9cI want to talk to you. You are\r\nperhaps in a hurry, but please, be so kind, spare me two minutes,\xe2\x80\x9d and\r\nhe drew up a chair for her.\r\n\r\nSonia sat down again, and again timidly she took a hurried, frightened\r\nlook at the two ladies, and dropped her eyes. Raskolnikov\xe2\x80\x99s pale face\r\nflushed, a shudder passed over him, his eyes glowed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMother,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, firmly and insistently, \xe2\x80\x9cthis is Sofya Semyonovna\r\nMarmeladov, the daughter of that unfortunate Mr. Marmeladov, who was run\r\nover yesterday before my eyes, and of whom I was just telling you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nPulcheria Alexandrovna glanced at Sonia, and slightly screwed up\r\nher eyes. In spite of her embarrassment before Rodya\xe2\x80\x99s urgent and\r\nchallenging look, she could not deny herself that satisfaction. Dounia\r\ngazed gravely and intently into the poor girl\xe2\x80\x99s face, and scrutinised\r\nher with perplexity. Sonia, hearing herself introduced, tried to raise\r\nher eyes again, but was more embarrassed than ever.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI wanted to ask you,\xe2\x80\x9d said Raskolnikov, hastily, \xe2\x80\x9chow things were\r\narranged yesterday. You were not worried by the police, for instance?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, that was all right... it was too evident, the cause of death...\r\nthey did not worry us... only the lodgers are angry.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAt the body\xe2\x80\x99s remaining so long. You see it is hot now. So that,\r\nto-day, they will carry it to the cemetery, into the chapel, until\r\nto-morrow. At first Katerina Ivanovna was unwilling, but now she sees\r\nherself that it\xe2\x80\x99s necessary...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo-day, then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe begs you to do us the honour to be in the church to-morrow for the\r\nservice, and then to be present at the funeral lunch.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe is giving a funeral lunch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes... just a little.... She told me to thank you very much for helping\r\nus yesterday. But for you, we should have had nothing for the funeral.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAll at once her lips and chin began trembling, but, with an effort, she\r\ncontrolled herself, looking down again.\r\n\r\nDuring the conversation, Raskolnikov watched her carefully. She had a\r\nthin, very thin, pale little face, rather irregular and angular, with a\r\nsharp little nose and chin. She could not have been called pretty, but\r\nher blue eyes were so clear, and when they lighted up, there was such\r\na kindliness and simplicity in her expression that one could not help\r\nbeing attracted. Her face, and her whole figure indeed, had another\r\npeculiar characteristic. In spite of her eighteen years, she looked\r\nalmost a little girl--almost a child. And in some of her gestures, this\r\nchildishness seemed almost absurd.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut has Katerina Ivanovna been able to manage with such small means?\r\nDoes she even mean to have a funeral lunch?\xe2\x80\x9d Raskolnikov asked,\r\npersistently keeping up the conversation.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe coffin will be plain, of course... and everything will be plain, so\r\nit won\xe2\x80\x99t cost much. Katerina Ivanovna and I have reckoned it all out, so\r\nthat there will be enough left... and Katerina Ivanovna was very anxious\r\nit should be so. You know one can\xe2\x80\x99t... it\xe2\x80\x99s a comfort to her... she is\r\nlike that, you know....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI understand, I understand... of course... why do you look at my room\r\nlike that? My mother has just said it is like a tomb.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou gave us everything yesterday,\xe2\x80\x9d Sonia said suddenly, in reply, in a\r\nloud rapid whisper; and again she looked down in confusion. Her lips\r\nand chin were trembling once more. She had been struck at once\r\nby Raskolnikov\xe2\x80\x99s poor surroundings, and now these words broke out\r\nspontaneously. A silence followed. There was a light in Dounia\xe2\x80\x99s eyes,\r\nand even Pulcheria Alexandrovna looked kindly at Sonia.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cRodya,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, getting up, \xe2\x80\x9cwe shall have dinner together, of\r\ncourse. Come, Dounia.... And you, Rodya, had better go for a little\r\nwalk, and then rest and lie down before you come to see us.... I am\r\nafraid we have exhausted you....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, yes, I\xe2\x80\x99ll come,\xe2\x80\x9d he answered, getting up fussily. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I have\r\nsomething to see to.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut surely you will have dinner together?\xe2\x80\x9d cried Razumihin, looking in\r\nsurprise at Raskolnikov. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you mean?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, yes, I am coming... of course, of course! And you stay a minute.\r\nYou do not want him just now, do you, mother? Or perhaps I am taking him\r\nfrom you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, no, no. And will you, Dmitri Prokofitch, do us the favour of dining\r\nwith us?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPlease do,\xe2\x80\x9d added Dounia.\r\n\r\nRazumihin bowed, positively radiant. For one moment, they were all\r\nstrangely embarrassed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood-bye, Rodya, that is till we meet. I do not like saying good-bye.\r\nGood-bye, Nastasya. Ah, I have said good-bye again.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nPulcheria Alexandrovna meant to greet Sonia, too; but it somehow failed\r\nto come off, and she went in a flutter out of the room.\r\n\r\nBut Avdotya Romanovna seemed to await her turn, and following her mother\r\nout, gave Sonia an attentive, courteous bow. Sonia, in confusion, gave\r\na hurried, frightened curtsy. There was a look of poignant discomfort\r\nin her face, as though Avdotya Romanovna\xe2\x80\x99s courtesy and attention were\r\noppressive and painful to her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDounia, good-bye,\xe2\x80\x9d called Raskolnikov, in the passage. \xe2\x80\x9cGive me your\r\nhand.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, I did give it to you. Have you forgotten?\xe2\x80\x9d said Dounia, turning\r\nwarmly and awkwardly to him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNever mind, give it to me again.\xe2\x80\x9d And he squeezed her fingers warmly.\r\n\r\nDounia smiled, flushed, pulled her hand away, and went off quite happy.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCome, that\xe2\x80\x99s capital,\xe2\x80\x9d he said to Sonia, going back and looking\r\nbrightly at her. \xe2\x80\x9cGod give peace to the dead, the living have still to\r\nlive. That is right, isn\xe2\x80\x99t it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSonia looked surprised at the sudden brightness of his face. He looked\r\nat her for some moments in silence. The whole history of the dead father\r\nfloated before his memory in those moments....\r\n\r\n**
